Guidance Is a Creative Act, Not Mere Bayan
Nasafi argues that divine guidance must be a creation, not just showing the way, using two Qur'anic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine guidance must be a creation in the heart and not merely an explanation, based on Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Guidance is a creation, not just clarification.

This passage from Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla tackles a fundamental dispute: Is Allah's guidance simply showing the way (bayan), or does it involve actually creating guidance in the heart? Using two powerful verses, Nasafi shows that if guidance were only explanation, the Quran would contradict itself. Let's follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the English translation. Notice the two verses cited: 'Innaka la tahdi man ahbabta' and 'faman yuridillahu an yahdiyahu yashrah sadrahu'.
Pay attention to the logical structure: claim, verse, reductio, conclusion.
2
Identify the Maturidi claim
Nasafi first states the Maturidi position: Allah is the Guide because He creates the act of guidance, and the Misguider because He creates misguidance. This is the foundational claim.
3
Examine the first proof from Surah al-Qasas
The verse 'Innaka la tahdi man ahbabta' shows that the Prophet cannot guide even those he loves. If guidance were only bayan, he would be able to. So there must be another kind of guidance beyond explanation.
This verse directly refutes the Mu'tazilite equation of guidance with bayan.
4
Examine the second proof from Surah al-An'am
The verse about expanded chests: if guidance were just da'wa and bayan, then everyone called would have an expanded chest. But the same verse speaks of a tight chest, which would be contradictory if guidance were only bayan. This proves that guidance and misguidance are creative acts that produce actual states.
The reductio shows the Mu'tazilite view leads to attributing impossible contradictions to Allah.
5
Understand the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that the Mu'tazilite interpretation leads to falsehood and disbelief because it forces a contradiction in Allah's actions and speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن لما أقمنا الدلالة على أن الله تعالى خالق أفعال العباد كان هادياً لتخليقه فعل الاهتداء، ومضلاً لتخليقه فعل الضلال. مناقشة كلام المعتزلة] ثم الذي يبطل جميع ما ذهبوا إليه من التأويلات قوله تعالى مخاطباً لنبيه عليه السلام: إِنَّكَ لَا تَهْدِى مَنْ أَحْبَبْتَ وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يَهْدِى مَن يَشَاءُ ولو كان الهدى هو البيان لكان النبي عليه السلام يهدي من أحبه، فدل أن وراء البيان هداية أخرى وليس ذلك إلا ما قلنا يدل على أن الله تعالى قال: فَمَن يُرِدِ اللهُ أَن يَهْدِيَهُ يَشْرَحْ صَدْرَهُ لِلْإِسْلَامِ ولو كان المراد من الهداية الدعوة وبيان الطريق ينبغي أن يقال كل من دعاه الله للإيمان وبين له طريق الدين فهو مشروح الصدر، فيصير قوله تعالى: يَجْعَلْ صَدْرَهُ ضَيِّقًا حَرَجًا باطلاً كذباً وهو كفر، وكذا كل من يسميه الله تعالى ضالاً ينبغي أن يجعل صدره ضيقاً حرجاً وكذا كل من يجده ضالاً، ثم إن الله تعالى بين الطريق لكل كافر فإذا لم يسلم يجده ضالاً ويسميه فينبغي أن يجعل صدره ضيقاً حرجاً، فإذا كل كافر يشرح الله صدره لأنه هداه ويضيق صدره لأنه أضله وفيه وصف الله تعالى لفعل ماهو محال، وكذا تقسيم الله تعالى الخلق قسمين: أحدهما شرح صدره، والآخر ضيق صدره باطل وهذا كله كفر.
And we, when we established the proof that Allah Most High is the Creator of the acts of the servants, He is the Guide by His creation of the act of guidance, and the Misguider by His creation of the act of misguidance. [Discussion of the Mu'tazilite speech] Then that which invalidates all the interpretations they have gone to is His saying, addressing His Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills.' If guidance were mere explanation (bayan), the Prophet would guide whom he loves. So it indicates that beyond explanation there is another guidance, and that is nothing but what we said. It indicates that Allah Most High said: 'Whomever Allah wills to guide, He expands his chest for Islam.' If what is intended by guidance was the call and showing the way, it would be necessary to say that everyone whom Allah calls to faith and shows the way of religion is expanded of chest. Then His saying 'He makes his chest tight and constricted' would become false and a lie, and that is disbelief. Similarly, everyone whom Allah Most High calls misguided, it would be necessary to make his chest tight and constricted, and likewise everyone whom He finds misguided. Then Allah Most High showed the way to every disbeliever, so if he does not accept Islam, He finds him misguided and calls him misguided, so it would be necessary to make his chest tight and constricted. Thus every disbeliever would have Allah expand his chest because He guided him, and constrict his chest because He misguided him—and that involves describing Allah with an impossible act. Likewise, Allah's division of creation into two groups: one whose chest He expanded and the other whose chest He constricted, would be false, and all of this is disbelief.
Source pages p. 991

Commentary
This passage is a structured proof (dalil) that divine guidance is a creative act, not mere communication. The author first asserts the Maturidi position: Allah creates both the act of guidance and the act of misguidance. Then he presents a refutation of Mu'tazilite ta'wilat. The key argument: If guidance were only bayan (making the truth clear), the Prophet would be able to guide anyone he loved, but the verse 'Innaka la tahdi man ahbabta' (Qasas 56) clearly negates that. Therefore, there must be a 'guidance beyond bayan'—namely, Allah's creation of guidance in the heart. The argument then uses the verse 'faman yuridillahu an yahdiyahu yashrah sadrahu' (An'am 125): if guidance were just da'wa (calling) and bayan, then everyone called would have a cheerful chest. But the same verse says that for some He makes the chest tight (haraj). Thus, if guidance were merely call + bayan, the description of a tight chest would be contradictory and imply that Allah lies—which is impossible. Consequently, guidance and misguidance must be creative acts that produce actual spiritual states. The passage concludes by rejecting the Mu'tazilite position as leading to absurdities and disbelief.

Key Terms
الهدى
البيان
شرح الصدر
ضيق الصدر
الاهتداء
الضلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Guidance in the Quran means only showing the way or explaining the truth (bayan).
Correction: The verses show that guidance also involves a creative act that brings about actual spiritual states like an expanded chest, which mere explanation cannot achieve.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why cannot divine guidance be only 'bayan' (making clear)?
A) Because the Prophet successfully guided many people
B) Because the Qur'an says 'You do not guide whom you love'—so the Prophet cannot guide even when he explains
C) Because all people are equally guided
D) Because guidance is only for prophets

Key Takeaway
Divine guidance is a creative act of Allah in the heart, not merely showing the truth, as proven by Quranic verses that would otherwise contradict each other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sincerely tried to guide someone to Islam but they remained stubborn, did you feel that your effort was wasted? How does Nasafi's argument that guidance is Allah's creation, not your explanation, challenge your sense of responsibility and reliance on Allah? What can you actually do now that you know only Allah creates guidance?
?
Read verse (6:125) again: 'Whomever Allah wills to guide, He expands his chest for Islam.' Honestly examine your own heart: do you feel an expansion for faith, or a tightness? If you feel tightness, does that alarm you about your spiritual state? What concrete step will you take today to sincerely ask Allah to expand your chest, with full awareness that only He can do it?
?
Nasafi says that if guidance were mere explanation, describing a disbeliever as both guided (because called) and misguided would be an impossible description of Allah's actions. Does this deepen your awe that Allah's attributes are perfect and without contradiction? How does this truth compel you to submit your intellect to revelation, even when it seems hard? Will you accept that Allah's actions are beyond full human comprehension?

The Dilemma of Absolute Promises and the Role of Specification
Refutation and defense of specification principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi argument against taking absolute promises and general words literally, and the principle that apparent meaning can be overridden by evidence of specification.

Core Idea
Absolute promises are always implicitly conditioned; the apparent meaning is not final when evidence of specification exists.

In this passage, the author tackles a key debate: do absolute promises and general words imply universal application? Using the story of Adam and the verse on forgiveness, he shows that taking words literally leads to absurdities. He then defends the Maturidi position that the apparent meaning is not definitive when there is evidence of specification, and clarifies that his school does not deny the apparent meaning but allows for interpretation when supported by evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the English translation. Try to grasp the overall flow of the argument before analyzing details.
The passage is dense; it helps to read it twice.
2
Identify the two key dilemmas
Find the two examples: the story of Adam (uncovered despite promise) and the verse 'Allah forgives all sins.' Notice how each creates a dilemma for those who take the words absolutely.
The dilemmas are structured as 'if yes then X, if no then Y'.
3
Understand the author's rebuttal
Notice how the author rejects the absolute interpretation and argues that the promise had an implicit restriction. Then see how he refutes the claim that Maturidis always take apparent meaning as final.
The rebuttal cites examples from Maturidi books where speakers are believed when they claim a non-apparent meaning.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that Allah's evidence of specification indicates His intention from the start. Consider why this is important for understanding revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الزلة عرى على ما قال تعالى: وَطَفِقَا يَعْصِفَانِ عَلَيْهِمَا مِن وَرَقِ الجَنَّةِ. أكان ذلك الوعد المطلق تناول حال وجود الزلة أم لا؟ فإن قال: تناول فقد ظهر كذب الله تعالى حيث وعد له أن لا يعرى وقد عرى. وإن قال لم يتناول حال الزلة، فقد زعم أن الوعد المطلق العاري عن القيد كان المراد منه القيد بحالة، وفيه إبطال مذهبهم وفساد القول بدلالة الصيغة المتعرية عن دليل الخصوص والقيد على إرادة العموم والإطلاق. وكذا يقال أليس أن الله تعالى قال: قُلْ يَا عِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ لَا تَقْنَطُوا مِن رَّحْمَةِ اللَّهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَغْفِرُ الذُّنُوبَ جَمِيعًا. أيغفر كل ذنب أم لا؟ ولم يقترن به قيد ولا تخصيص ذنب فإن قالوا: نعم. أبطلوا مذهبهم وخرجوا أيضا عن الإجماع. وإن قالوا: لا. قيل هل يصير الله تعالى كاذبًا بذلك؟ فإن قالوا: نعم. كفروا. وإن قالوا: لا أبطلوا مذهبهم. ولولا مخافة الإطالة لبينت بعض الدلائل في مسألة العموم وكشفت عما يموهون على الضعفة بإيراد بعض مسائل أصحابنا ويصورون عندهم أن من مذهب أصحابنا القول بوجوب اعتقاد شمول حكم العام فيما يتناوله بلفظه، والشهادة على الله تعالى أنه أراد به الكل والحجر عليه عن إرادة خصوص فيه أو قيد، غير أن ما شرطنا في أول الكتاب من الاجتناب عن الإطالة منعنا عن الاشتغال بذلك، وكيف يدعي أحد ذلك على أصحابنا وقد يوجد في كتبهم ما يتعذر إحصاؤه من المسائل أن من تكلم بكلام وقال: عنيت به غير الظاهر الذي وضع له في حقيقة اللغة أنه يصدق إذا كان غير متهم في ذلك بأن شدد بما أخبر على نفسه والتزم به الضرر وإنما لا يصدقه القاضي فما ينتفع به لو فيما يدعيه من إرادته خلاف الظاهر، فكان هذا مذهبًا منهم أن من تكلم بلفظ ثم عني به ما يحتمله اللفظ يصدق، وإن كان فيه عدول عن ظاهرة إذا لم يكن متهما في ذلك، وفيه دليل أنهم ما جعلوا ظاهر اللفظ عند تعريه عن دليل يدل على أن المراد به خلاف الظاهر دليلاً على إرادة الظاهر، إذ لو كان كذلك لما قبل منه قوله أني عنيت خلاف الظاهر وإن لم يكن متهمًا في ذلك، كمن ادعى ما لا يحتمله اللفظ لا يصدق وإن لم يكن متهمًا في ذلك. ثم الله تعالى غير متهم فيما يقيم من دلالة الخصوص ينبغي أن يكون ذلك دليل إرادة الخصوص من وقت نزوله، والله أعلم.
The sin was exposed upon what He said Almighty: "And they began to cover themselves with leaves of Paradise." Was that absolute promise applicable at the time of the sin or not? If he says: it applied, then the lying of Allah Almighty has appeared because He promised him that he would not be uncovered and he was uncovered. And if he says: it did not apply at the time of the sin, then he claimed that the absolute promise free from restriction was intended to be restricted by a state, and in that is the nullification of their view and the corruption of the statement that the absolute form free from evidence of specification and restriction indicates intention of generality and absoluteness. Similarly, it is said: Did not Allah Almighty say: "Say: O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of Allah; indeed Allah forgives all sins." Does He forgive every sin or not? And no restriction nor specification of a sin was attached to it. If they say: yes, they nullify their own view and also depart from consensus. And if they say: no, it is said: would Allah thereby become a liar? If they say: yes, they disbelieve. And if they say: no, they nullify their view. And were it not for fear of prolixity, I would have clarified some proofs concerning the issue of generality and uncovered what they obscure to the weak by presenting some issues of our companions and they depict to them that from the doctrine of our companions is the obligation to believe in the inclusiveness of the ruling of the general with respect to what it covers by its wording, and bearing testimony against Allah Almighty that He intended by it everything, and preventing Him from intending any specification in it or restriction, except that what we stipulated at the beginning of the book of avoiding prolixity prevented us from occupying ourselves with that. And how can anyone claim that about our companions when there are found in their books countless issues that whoever speaks a word and says: I meant by it other than the apparent for which it was placed in the reality of language, that he is believed if he is not accused in that, because he has made severe what he informed about himself and committed to the harm, and the judge does not believe him in what is beneficial to him in what he claims of intending contrary to the apparent. So this was a doctrine from them that whoever speaks a word and then means by it what the word can bear, he is believed, even if there is in it a departure from its apparent meaning, provided he is not accused in that. And in this is evidence that they did not make the apparent meaning of the wording, when it is free from evidence showing that the intended meaning is contrary to the apparent, as evidence for intending the apparent; for if it were so, his saying "I intended contrary to the apparent" would not be accepted, even if he is not accused in that, like one who claims what the wording cannot bear is not believed, even if he is not accused in that. Then Allah Almighty is not accused in what He establishes of evidence of specification; it should be that that is evidence of intending specification from the time of its revelation, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 1069

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who claim that absolute promises (wa'd mutlaq) must apply in all circumstances, and a defense of the Maturidi position on the interpretation of general words (umum) and the possibility of specification (takhsis). The author begins by referring to the story of Adam in Paradise: Allah promised Adam that he would not be uncovered, but after eating from the tree he became uncovered. The author poses a dilemma: either the absolute promise applied during the sin, which would imply Allah's promise was false (since Adam was uncovered), or it did not apply, meaning the promise was implicitly restricted to a state before the sin. The latter is the correct view, and the former leads to absurdity. The author then raises a similar argument from the Quranic verse "Allah forgives all sins" — if taken absolutely, it would mean every sin is forgiven, which contradicts consensus; if not, then Allah would be lying unless the verse is restricted. The author then criticizes those who falsely attribute to his school (Ashabuna) the view that the apparent meaning (zahir) of a general word must always be taken as comprehensive and that Allah cannot intend specification. He refutes this by citing their own books: they hold that if a speaker says a word and claims he meant a possible but non-apparent meaning, he is believed if he is not accused of lying, provided he incurs some harm or difficulty. This shows that they do not treat the apparent meaning as definitive when there is evidence of specification. The author concludes that since Allah is not accused of deception, His evidence of specification should be accepted as indicating that He intended the specific meaning from the time of revelation.

Key Terms
الزلة (al-zalla) - sin/slip
وعد (wa'd) - promise
عموم (umum) - generality
خصوص (khusus) - specification
ظاهر (zahir) - apparent meaning
صيغة عامة (sigha 'amma) - general form
مطلق (mutlaq) - absolute
مقيد (muqayyad) - restricted
دليل الخصوص (dalil al-khusus) - evidence of specification
إرادة (irada) - intention
تصديق (tasdiq) - belief in a claim

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidis reject the apparent meaning of general words absolutely and believe that the apparent meaning must always be taken as comprehensive.
Correction: The Maturidis accept the apparent meaning unless there is evidence to the contrary. They allow for interpretation when the speaker intends a possible non-apparent meaning, especially if the speaker is not accused of lying and incurs some harm.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if one claims that the absolute promise in the story of Adam applied during the sin?
A) It shows Allah's promise was conditional.
B) It shows Allah became a liar.
C) It shows the promise was not absolute.
D) It shows the general word indicates specification.

Key Takeaway
The apparent meaning of a general word is not binding when there is evidence of specification, and Allah's own evidence for specification must be accepted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'Allah forgives all sins,' do you treat it as a license to sin repeatedly? How does this lesson's discussion on specification expose the danger of taking that verse out of context? What evidence from the passage shows that the verse is not absolute? Will you stop using it to justify disobedience and instead seek forgiveness with sincere repentance?
?
If someone made you a promise that later seemed broken, would you be quick to accuse them of lying? How does Adam's example teach you to trust God's promises even when your circumstances appear contradictory? This week, will you commit to trusting God's word even when it seems challenged by reality?
?
The author explains that if a speaker claims a non-apparent meaning, they are believed if not accused. How often do you assume the worst about others' intentions when their words seem unclear? Are you willing to extend the same charity to others that you would want for yourself? What specific step will you take this week to seek the intended meaning before judging someone's statement?

Consensus Proved Through Ali's Authority
The author argues for consensus using Ali's authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Ali’s acknowledgment of Abu Bakr’s caliphate as a proof for the binding nature of consensus.

Core Idea
Ali’s approved pledge proves consensus is binding.

The author begins by stating that consensus is a binding proof like the textual proof (nass). He then chooses not to repeat the well-known proofs for consensus, but instead presents a specific argument that uses the authority of Ali (RA). Since the Rawafid consider Ali’s opinion as authoritative, and it is established through mutawatir transmission that Ali pledged allegiance to Abu Bakr and acknowledged his caliphate, this serves as a sufficient proof for the validity of Abu Bakr’s caliphate and, by extension, the binding nature of consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully.
Notice that the author does not repeat all proofs; he focuses on one argument.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the claim (consensus is binding), the proof (Ali’s pledge), and the premise (Ali’s opinion is authoritative for the opponent).
This argument works because the opponents accept Ali’s authority.
3
Reflect on the polemical context
Consider why the author addresses the Rawafid specifically and how this argument refutes their rejection of consensus.
The argument assumes that if Ali agreed, then consensus was achieved.

الإجماع حجة ملزمة كالنص: فلو أنهم مالوا إلى إنكار كون الإجماع حجة فنثبت عليهم بالدلائل المشهورة التي أوردها أئمة الدين في إثبات كون الإجماع حجة، لا معنى لاشتغالنا في هذا الكتاب بذلك لشهرتها في كل كتاب صنف في أصول الفقه، ومن أراد الوقوف عليها لا يعدمها ولا يتعذر عليه الظفر بها. على أن رأي عليه وقوله عندهم حجة، وقد ثبت بالنقل المتواتر الذي ينسب جاحده إلى العناد والمكابرة بيعته أبا بكر واعترافه بخلافته، فيكون قوله حجة كافية لصحة خلافته، ولا يقع لهم فيما يزعمون أن الإجماع مع مخالفة البعض غير منعقد (ويوهم أن بعضا خالف ولم يعلم يقينا عدم مخالفة البعض) لأن خلاف البعض لو توهم فعلی به ثبت وفاقه وقوله عندكم حجة كافية، ثم نقول لو وجد خلاف البعض لظهر إذ لا يتوهم في العادات الجارية خلاف من يعد بخلافه خلافا في مثل هذه الحادثة ثم تتكتم ولا تشتهر ، ولو جاز ذا لجاز أن يزعم ملحد أن القرآن لعله عورض ولم ينقل معارضة، وكذا معجزة كل نبي فيصير ذلك طريقًا لإبطال الرسالات وتعطيل المعجزات والآيات التي أتى بها الرسل عليهم السلام، وذا كفر وباطل فكذا ما أدى إليه، بل فيه إنكار الشاهدات وجحد الضروريات وإفساد الألسنة واللغات، إذ ما من كلام يتكلم به إلا ويمكن لقائل أن يقول إن ما ذكرت من الألفاظ ليست بدلالة على ما قصدت إليه من المعاني إذ لم يثبت ذلك باتفاق أهل اللسان أو مساعدة أهل البلدة أو القبيلة إذ يتوهم أن بعضهم يجعل هذه الألفاظ عبارات عن أضداد هذه المعاني، وما هذا سبيله لا يجوز التفات إليه ولا الاشتغال بجواب من جعله معلولاً عليه لتأييد نحلته وتقوية رأيه ومذهبه.
Consensus is a binding proof like the textual proof: If they incline to deny that consensus is a proof, we will prove it to them by the well-known proofs that the imams of the religion have presented in establishing that consensus is a proof. There is no meaning to our occupying ourselves with that in this book due to its fame in every book written on the principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh). Whoever wants to examine them will not lack them, nor will it be difficult for him to obtain them. Moreover, the opinion of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and his statement is considered a proof according to them. It has been established through mutawatir transmission (that attributes its denier to stubbornness and obstinacy) that he pledged allegiance to Abu Bakr and acknowledged his caliphate. Thus his statement is a sufficient proof for the validity of his caliphate. And it will not occur to them, in what they claim, that consensus with opposition of some is not concluded (and they suggest that some opposed and it is not known with certainty that there was no opposition of some) because the opposition of some, if imagined, then by it his agreement is established and his statement is a sufficient proof according to you. Then we say: If the opposition of some existed, it would have appeared, since it cannot be imagined in customary practices that the opposition of one whose opposition is considered a valid opposition in such an incident would then be concealed and not become famous. And if this were permissible, it would be permissible for an atheist to claim that the Qur'an might have been challenged but the challenge was not transmitted, and likewise the miracle of every prophet, and that would become a way to invalidate the messages and nullify the miracles and signs that the messengers (peace be upon them) brought. That is unbelief and falsehood, so likewise what leads to it. Rather, in it is the denial of witnessed facts, the rejection of necessities, and the corruption of languages and tongues, for there is no speech spoken except that a speaker can say that the words you mentioned are not indicative of the meanings you intended, since that has not been established by the agreement of the people of the language or the assistance of the people of the town or tribe, because it is imagined that some of them use these words as expressions for meanings opposite to these. And what is of this nature, no attention should be paid to it, nor should one occupy oneself with answering one who makes it a proof to support his sect and strengthen his opinion and doctrine.
Source pages p. 1138

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation of doubts regarding the binding nature of consensus (ijma'). The author first states that the proofs for consensus are well-known, so he will not repeat them. He then provides a specific argument: since the Rawafid accept Ali's opinion as authoritative, and Ali acknowledged Abu Bakr's caliphate through mutawatir reports, that acknowledgment is sufficient proof. The author then refutes the objection that consensus might not be binding if some dissented in secret. He argues that if such secret opposition existed, it would have become public knowledge. To allow the possibility of secret opposition would lead to absurd consequences, such as denying the Qur'an or miracles on the grounds that counter-evidence might have been hidden, which is self-defeating. He concludes that such sophistical doubts should be ignored.

Key Terms
إجماع
نص
تواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Consensus cannot be a proof because the Rawafid reject it.
Correction: The author shows that even the Rawafid's own authority (Ali) accepted the consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate, thus demonstrating consensus is binding.

Checkpoint
What does the author use as proof for consensus?
A) The well-known proofs from usul al-fiqh books
B) Ali's pledge of allegiance to Abu Bakr
C) The consensus of all Muslims
D) A revelation from the Qur'an

Key Takeaway
The author uses Ali's acknowledged authority to prove that consensus is binding, specifically by citing his acceptance of Abu Bakr's caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disagree with a clear consensus of scholars, is it because you have a valid proof, or because your desires are leading you? Will you submit to the authority of the Muslim community's agreement, even when it is hard to accept?
?
The author uses Ali's acceptance of a difficult reality to prove consensus. What is one thing you are refusing to accept that the Muslim community has agreed upon? What is preventing you from following Ali's example?

Refuting the Objection of Hidden Opposition
The author refutes the objection of hidden opposition with a reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reductio ad absurdum argument against the objection that hidden opposition could invalidate consensus.

Core Idea
If hidden opposition could invalidate consensus, all knowledge could be doubted.

After presenting a positive proof for consensus, the author anticipates an objection: what if some people opposed secretly, so that consensus was not truly achieved? The author refutes this by showing that if such hidden opposition were possible, it would lead to absurd consequences, such as the ability to deny the Qur'an or miracles on the grounds that counter-evidence might have been hidden. This reductio demonstrates that the objection is invalid and should be dismissed.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Identify the objection that hidden opposition prevents consensus from being concluded.
The opponent suggests that some may have opposed but their opposition is unknown.
2
Analyze the author's counterargument
The author argues that if the opposition existed, it would have become known because of the importance of the event.
The event of Abu Bakr's caliphate was major; any significant opposition would have been recorded.
3
Understand the reductio
The author extends the logic to show that if hidden opposition is allowed, it opens the door to denying any transmitted knowledge, including the Qur'an and prophets' miracles.
This leads to absurdity and unbelief.
4
Conclude the author's point
Therefore, such sophistical objections should be ignored.

Various Meanings of 'Mawla'
Author enumerates meanings of 'mawla' and concludes they don't support caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the word 'mawla' has multiple meanings in Arabic, including wali, muhibb, jar, nasir, and sihr, and that none of these meanings inherently imply political succession (caliphate or imamate).

Core Idea
Mawla has many meanings, but none mean 'caliph'.

The word 'mawla' is rich in meaning. In this passage, the author lists several possible interpretations—guardian, friend, neighbor, supporter, in-law—and emphasizes that these do not establish the claim of political succession for Ali. We will explore these meanings through linguistic evidence and poetic examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Notice the author’s enumeration of meanings.
2
Identify the five meanings
List the five meanings of 'mawla' mentioned: guardian (wali), loving friend (muhibb/muwali), neighbor (jar), in-law (sihr), and supporter (nasir). Note that 'nasir' appears only at the end of this section.
The first four are explicitly illustrated with examples.
3
Examine the poetic evidence
Read the two poetic examples: one for 'neighbor' and one for 'in-law'. Notice how each context clarifies the meaning.
Poetry is used to demonstrate linguistic usage.
4
Understand the conclusion on caliphate
The author states that none of these meanings are built upon the caliphate and imamate. This is a key refutation of the sectarian claim.
This sets up the next lesson's selection of the appropriate meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويذكر ويراد به الولي، والمحب الموالي، وقد روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: مزينة وجهينة وأسلم وعقار موالي الله ورسوله (۱) أي محبون موالون(٢) الله ورسوله، ويذكر ويراد به الجار. قال مربع بن دعدعة الكلابي - وكان جاور كليب بن يربوع فأحمد جوارهم:
جزى الله خيرا والجزاء يكفه
كليب بن يربوع وزادهم حمدا
هم حاطونا (۳) بالنفوس وألجموا
إلى نصر مولاهم مسومة جردا
ويذكر ويراد به الصهر قال المختار بن يزيد بن قيس الكلابي:
•
فلا تنسين النافعين كليهما
وهذا الذي في السوق مولى بني بدر
وكان الرجل صهرا لبني بدر
وشيء من هذه المعاني لا تبنى على الخلافة والإمامة ثم ما يليق بالحديث من هذه المعاني: "الناصر"، أي من كنت ناصره على دينه وحاميا له بباطني وظاهري فعلي ناصره وحاميه بباطنه وظاهره؛ فيكون دليلاً على طهارة سيرة علي الله وعلو رتبته إذ ليس كل ناصر بظاهره هذا رتبته في باطنه إذ قد يفعل ذلك طلبًا للرياء والسمعة وابتغاء المال والفوز بالغنائم، ويحتمل أن يكون (٤) معناه من كنت محبوبًا عنده فعلي محبوب عنده، وفائدة تخصيصه بذلك أنه عليه السلام ربما علم أن قوما ممن أضلهم الله تعالى وأعمى أبصارهم سيطعنون عليه، ويزعمون (٦) أنه خرج من الدين وفارقه، وحكّم في أمر الله غير الله وسقطت بذلك ولايته وزال ولاؤه، فقال عليه السلام ذلك ليدل على بطلان قول أولئك.
And it is mentioned and intended by it the guardian, and the loving friend, and it has been narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Muzaynah, Juhaynah, Aslam, and 'Akkar are the mawali (plural of mawla) of Allah and His Messenger' (1) meaning lovers, friends (2) of Allah and His Messenger. And it is mentioned and intended by it the neighbor. Marba' ibn Da'dh'a al-Kilabi said – and he had neighbored Kulayb ibn Yarbu' and praised their neighborliness: 'May Allah reward good, and the reward suffices, Kulayb ibn Yarbu', and increase them in praise. They protected us with their souls and bridled, for the victory of their mawla, marked horses.' And it is mentioned and intended by it the in-law. al-Mukhtar ibn Yazid ibn Qays al-Kilabi said: 'Do not forget both benefactors, and this one in the market is the mawla of Banu Badr.' And the man was an in-law of Banu Badr. And something of these meanings is not built upon the caliphate and the imamate. Then what is suitable from these meanings for the hadith is 'the supporter', i.e., whoever I am his supporter in his religion and protector for him inwardly and outwardly, then 'Ali is his supporter and his protector inwardly and outwardly. So it is evidence for the purity of 'Ali's conduct and the highness of his rank, since not every supporter outwardly has this rank inwardly, because he may do that seeking hypocrisy and reputation and seeking wealth and winning spoils. And it is possible that (4) its meaning is: whoever I am beloved to him, then 'Ali is beloved to him. And the benefit of specifying him with that is that he, peace be upon him, perhaps knew that some people from among those whom Allah led astray and blinded their eyes would slander him and claim (6) that he left the religion and separated from it, and judged in Allah's matter other than Allah, and thus his guardianship (wilayah) fell and his friendship (wala') ceased, so he said that to indicate the falsehood of the statement of those.
Source pages p. 1142

Commentary
This passage begins a linguistic and theological analysis of the word 'mawla' as it appears in the famous hadith 'Whoever I am his mawla, 'Ali is his mawla.' The author first lists several meanings of the word mawla: it can mean 'wali' (guardian), 'muhibb' (loving friend), 'jar' (neighbor), 'nasir' (supporter), and 'sihr' (in-law). He provides examples from poetry and from a hadith about tribes to illustrate these meanings. He then argues that none of these meanings, except one, support the Rafidah's claim that the hadith establishes the caliphate or imamate of 'Ali. The appropriate meaning for this specific hadith is 'al-nasir' (the supporter). The author explains that the Prophet, by saying 'Whoever I am his supporter in his religion and protector inwardly and outwardly, then 'Ali is his supporter and protector', intends to demonstrate 'Ali's high rank and pure conduct. The Prophet foresaw that some misguided people would later slander 'Ali and claim that he had left the religion, so this hadith serves as a refutation of those claims. An additional possible interpretation is that the hadith means 'whoever I am beloved to him, then 'Ali is beloved to him,' highlighting 'Ali's closeness to the Prophet. Throughout, the author emphasizes that the hadith is not a designation of political succession (imama or khilafa), but rather a statement of spiritual support and love.

مولى
ولي
محب
جار
صهر
خلافة
إمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu' is a clear designation of Ali as the political successor (caliph) of the Prophet.
Correction: The author shows that 'mawla' has many meanings, none of which inherently imply political succession. The hadith must be interpreted in context.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a meaning of 'mawla' mentioned in this passage?
A) Guardian (wali)
B) Leader (khalifa)
C) Loving friend (muhibb)
D) In-law (sihr)

Key Takeaway
The word 'mawla' in the hadith has multiple possible meanings, and none of them directly establish the caliphate or imamate of Ali.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
هل تتبنى معنىً لكلمة 'مولى' يريحك عاطفياً أو طائفياً دون أن تبحث عن المعنى الذي قصده النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الحديث؟ ماذا ستغير في فهمك لو ثبت أن المعنى هو 'المحب الموالي'؟
?
أنت أمام نص شرعي يحتمل أكثر من معنى، فهل تسارع إلى تفسيره بما يوافق هوى نفسك أو مذهبك؟ أم تقف متأدباً منتظراً الدليل؟ ما الذي يمنعك من الإنصاف؟
?
لو كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يريد أن ينص على خلافة علي بكلمة 'مولى'، فلماذا لم يقل 'خليفتي' أو 'إمامكم' بوضوح؟ ألا يدعوك هذا إلى مراجعة ما تظنه يقيناً؟

The Correct Meaning: 'Supporter'
Author selects 'nasir' as the intended meaning and explains the hadith's purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the most appropriate meaning of 'mawla' in the hadith is 'al-nasir' (the supporter), and that the hadith serves to affirm Ali's spiritual rank and refute future slander.

Core Idea
The hadith means 'supporter,' not 'successor'.

After discarding irrelevant meanings, the author selects 'al-nasir' (the supporter) as the intended meaning for the famous hadith. He explains that the Prophet foretold slander against Ali and used this hadith to uphold his honor and rank. We will explore this reasoning and an alternative interpretation of 'beloved'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the suitable meaning
Read the Arabic and translation starting from 'Then what is suitable...' Notice the author's choice of 'al-nasir'.
This is the author's main contribution to the interpretation.
2
Understand why 'nasir' fits
The author explains that 'nasir' means supporter in religion, both inwardly and outwardly. This fits the context of the Prophet's relationship with Ali.
It emphasizes sincerity, not outward show.
3
Note the alternative interpretation
The author also mentions an alternative: 'whoever I am beloved to him, then Ali is beloved to him.' This reinforces closeness.
Both interpretations avoid political claims.
4
Reflect on the purpose of the hadith
The Prophet said this to refute future slanderers who would claim Ali left the religion. The hadith affirms Ali's continued guardianship and friendship.
This shows the hadith is about defense, not succession.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويذكر ويراد به الولي، والمحب الموالي، وقد روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: مزينة وجهينة وأسلم وعقار موالي الله ورسوله (۱) أي محبون موالون(٢) الله ورسوله، ويذكر ويراد به الجار. قال مربع بن دعدعة الكلابي - وكان جاور كليب بن يربوع فأحمد جوارهم:
جزى الله خيرا والجزاء يكفه
كليب بن يربوع وزادهم حمدا
هم حاطونا (۳) بالنفوس وألجموا
إلى نصر مولاهم مسومة جردا
ويذكر ويراد به الصهر قال المختار بن يزيد بن قيس الكلابي:
•
فلا تنسين النافعين كليهما
وهذا الذي في السوق مولى بني بدر
وكان الرجل صهرا لبني بدر
وشيء من هذه المعاني لا تبنى على الخلافة والإمامة ثم ما يليق بالحديث من هذه المعاني: "الناصر"، أي من كنت ناصره على دينه وحاميا له بباطني وظاهري فعلي ناصره وحاميه بباطنه وظاهره؛ فيكون دليلاً على طهارة سيرة علي الله وعلو رتبته إذ ليس كل ناصر بظاهره هذا رتبته في باطنه إذ قد يفعل ذلك طلبًا للرياء والسمعة وابتغاء المال والفوز بالغنائم، ويحتمل أن يكون (٤) معناه من كنت محبوبًا عنده فعلي محبوب عنده، وفائدة تخصيصه بذلك أنه عليه السلام ربما علم أن قوما ممن أضلهم الله تعالى وأعمى أبصارهم سيطعنون عليه، ويزعمون (٦) أنه خرج من الدين وفارقه، وحكّم في أمر الله غير الله وسقطت بذلك ولايته وزال ولاؤه، فقال عليه السلام ذلك ليدل على بطلان قول أولئك.
And it is mentioned and intended by it the guardian, and the loving friend, and it has been narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Muzaynah, Juhaynah, Aslam, and 'Akkar are the mawali (plural of mawla) of Allah and His Messenger' (1) meaning lovers, friends (2) of Allah and His Messenger. And it is mentioned and intended by it the neighbor. Marba' ibn Da'dh'a al-Kilabi said – and he had neighbored Kulayb ibn Yarbu' and praised their neighborliness: 'May Allah reward good, and the reward suffices, Kulayb ibn Yarbu', and increase them in praise. They protected us with their souls and bridled, for the victory of their mawla, marked horses.' And it is mentioned and intended by it the in-law. al-Mukhtar ibn Yazid ibn Qays al-Kilabi said: 'Do not forget both benefactors, and this one in the market is the mawla of Banu Badr.' And the man was an in-law of Banu Badr. And something of these meanings is not built upon the caliphate and the imamate. Then what is suitable from these meanings for the hadith is 'the supporter', i.e., whoever I am his supporter in his religion and protector for him inwardly and outwardly, then 'Ali is his supporter and his protector inwardly and outwardly. So it is evidence for the purity of 'Ali's conduct and the highness of his rank, since not every supporter outwardly has this rank inwardly, because he may do that seeking hypocrisy and reputation and seeking wealth and winning spoils. And it is possible that (4) its meaning is: whoever I am beloved to him, then 'Ali is beloved to him. And the benefit of specifying him with that is that he, peace be upon him, perhaps knew that some people from among those whom Allah led astray and blinded their eyes would slander him and claim (6) that he left the religion and separated from it, and judged in Allah's matter other than Allah, and thus his guardianship (wilayah) fell and his friendship (wala') ceased, so he said that to indicate the falsehood of the statement of those.
Source pages p. 1142

Commentary
This passage begins a linguistic and theological analysis of the word 'mawla' as it appears in the famous hadith 'Whoever I am his mawla, 'Ali is his mawla.' The author first lists several meanings of the word mawla: it can mean 'wali' (guardian), 'muhibb' (loving friend), 'jar' (neighbor), 'nasir' (supporter), and 'sihr' (in-law). He provides examples from poetry and from a hadith about tribes to illustrate these meanings. He then argues that none of these meanings, except one, support the Rafidah's claim that the hadith establishes the caliphate or imamate of 'Ali. The appropriate meaning for this specific hadith is 'al-nasir' (the supporter). The author explains that the Prophet, by saying 'Whoever I am his supporter in his religion and protector inwardly and outwardly, then 'Ali is his supporter and protector', intends to demonstrate 'Ali's high rank and pure conduct. The Prophet foresaw that some misguided people would later slander 'Ali and claim that he had left the religion, so this hadith serves as a refutation of those claims. An additional possible interpretation is that the hadith means 'whoever I am beloved to him, then 'Ali is beloved to him,' highlighting 'Ali's closeness to the Prophet. Throughout, the author emphasizes that the hadith is not a designation of political succession (imama or khilafa), but rather a statement of spiritual support and love.

Key Terms
ناصر
مولى
محب
ولاية
ولاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith designates Ali as the political successor (imam) after the Prophet.
Correction: The author argues that the hadith means 'supporter' or 'beloved', not 'ruler'. Its purpose is to affirm Ali's spiritual rank and refute slander, not to establish political authority.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the primary benefit of specifying Ali in the hadith?
A) To designate him as the next caliph
B) To refute future slanderers who would claim Ali left the religion
C) To assert Ali's superiority over all other Companions
D) To establish a new religious law

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu' means 'whoever I am his supporter/beloved, Ali is his supporter/beloved', serving to defend Ali's honor and refute false claims, not to appoint him as caliph.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you support someone in the community, do you examine your own heart to see if your support is purely for Allah and His Messenger, or are you seeking recognition or personal benefit? How can you train yourself to be like Ali—consistent inside and out?
?
The Prophet foretold that people would slander Ali and claim he left the religion. Today, you may hear accusations against righteous people. Are you quick to believe such claims, or do you investigate and defend them as the Prophet did? What will you do the next time you hear a slander against a known believer?
?
If someone asked you today, 'Are you a supporter of Ali and his household?' would your answer be based on knowledge or on blind partisanship? How can you ensure your love for the Prophet's family is based on truth and not on imitation of others?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
5 min
Al-Maturidi on the Excuse of Ta'wil
Maturidi explains that ta'wil provides a greater excuse than simple ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Maturidi considers ta'wil a stronger excuse than simple ignorance for the one who sincerely interprets.

Core Idea
Ta'wil makes the practitioner feel commanded, removing the sense of omission.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi explains the unique nature of the excuse for those who engage in ta'wil (interpretation). He argues that when a person sincerely believes his interpretation is correct, it becomes like an act commanded by Allah in terms of his intention, providing an even stronger excuse than simple ignorance. This principle was used to justify the actions of the Companions in disputes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a very precise comparative structure here.
2
Identify the key terms
Identify the terms ta'wil (interpretation), jahala (ignorance), 'udhr (excuse), and kulfa (responsibility). These are central to the argument.
These terms recur in kalam discussions of accountability.
3
Understand the comparison
Maturidi compares ta'wil to two types of ignorance: ignorance of origin and mistake/forgetfulness. Determine why ta'wil is considered a stronger excuse.
The key is that ta'wil involves a belief of being commanded, which eliminates the sense of omission.
4
Apply to historical context
Consider how this principle applies to the Companions who fought each other in early Islamic conflicts. They acted based on their interpretations, not mere ignorance.
This shows the practical importance of Maturidi's argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا قال شيخنا أبو منصور الماتريدي رحمه الله - الأصل أن التأويل لأهله يجعله لما يرى عنده أنه حق كالمأمور به فهو أعظم من العذر، وأبلغ في معنى الجهالة التي تسقط الكلفة من الجهالة بأصل الخلقة والنشوء أو بالخطأ الذي اعتراه والسهو، لأن هذا النوع من الجهل عند نفسه علمه طلب الكشف والاستعانة بمن يثق به والاجتهاد في التيقظ والتحفظ، وليس مع التأويل في علمه ورأيه أنه قد بقي عليه حق لم يف به أو كان منه ما منعه عن حصول المقصود، فصار هذا لذلك أبلغ في العذر له وأعظم في معنى الجهالة لما معه بعض معاني الناسي عما يكون عليه من الحق في غيره، والله أعلم.
And for this reason our teacher Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The principle is that ta'wil (interpretation) for its practitioner makes what he thinks to be true like something commanded. So it is greater than an excuse, and more profound in the meaning of ignorance that drops responsibility than ignorance of the origin of creation and constitution, or the mistake that befell him and forgetfulness. Because this type of ignorance – in his own view – is that he knows the need for investigation and seeking help from those he trusts and striving in vigilance and caution. And with ta'wil, in his knowledge and opinion, it is not the case that there remains upon him a right he did not fulfill, or that something prevented him from attaining the goal. So this is therefore more profound as an excuse for him and greater in the meaning of ignorance because it carries some of the meaning of the one who forgets about what he should have done in other matters. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 1175

Commentary
This passage explains the profound nature of the excuse for those who engage in ta'wil (interpretation). Imam Maturidi argues that when a person makes a ta'wil and believes his action is correct, it becomes like an action commanded by Allah in terms of his intention. This provides a stronger excuse than simple ignorance (e.g., ignorance of the origin of creation) or a mistake accompanied by forgetfulness. Why? Because the person with ta'wil believes he is fulfilling a duty, so he has no sense of omission. This type of ignorance is coupled with a desire to seek truth, making the excuse even stronger. It ultimately excuses the Companions who fought because they interpreted the situation as requiring war, and they thought they were doing right.

Key Terms
تأويل
جهالة
عذر
كلفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that committing a wrong interpretation removes all blame entirely.
Correction: Maturidi does not say that ta'wil removes all blame; rather, it provides a strong excuse, but the action may still be incorrect. The practitioner is excused for his sincere effort, not declared blameless.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what makes ta'wil a stronger excuse than simple ignorance?
A) It involves a known truth.
B) The practitioner believes he is commanded, so he has no sense of omission.
C) It is always correct.
D) It is not an excuse at all.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi teaches that ta'wil, when sincerely held, provides a stronger excuse than ignorance because the practitioner believes he is commanded and feels no omission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever believed you were fulfilling a divine command, only to later discover you were mistaken? How does this passage challenge you to examine the sincerity of your own ta'wil, and what will you do now to ensure you are not merely comfortable but truly seeking the truth?
?
This lesson describes a person who, through ta'wil, feels no remaining right unfulfilled. Is there an area of your life where you justify your actions by 'interpretation' but deep down suspect you owe something to Allah or others? What step will you take tonight to address that?
?
Maturidi says the practitioner of ta'wil is aware of the need for investigation and caution. When you face a difficult religious or moral decision, do you actively seek trustworthy counsel and strive in vigilance, or do you rely on your own reasoning? How can you apply the lesson's standard to your next significant choice?
